This birding was for the Nevada Breeding Bird Atlas work conducted by Marshall Iliff and Brian Sullivan. We worked a different atlas block from the morning, this one at a ranch a few miles west of town. We asked permission to walk around and then split up and did separate wide loops. Marshall headed north and east and then walked the sagebrush margins to the west before looping back. Brian stayed closer to the ranchyard. Brian identified an Upland Sandpiper at the time, largely by call, but missed the vocal Long-billed Curlews and was unfamiliar with their call. I am not sure of Brian''s current opinion on Upland Sandpiper, but it would have represented a 3rd state record. We looked for his sandpiper for a while that afternoon and again the next morning to no avail. Start time, duration, and mileage are estimates.

Foraging actively in sahllow water and at times resting on a mud flat.  A few times I noted aggressive encounters with other male wigeons. ----Describe the habitat in which you observed the bird:--Medium sized man-made reservoir.  The flock was sticking close to the edge of the reservoir lined partially with cattail marsh and partially with an alkaline mud flat.  Surrounding matrix of of saltbush desert scrub, sedge meadows, and young ash groves.----Describe the bird's calls or sounds, if heard, including method of delivery, i.e., from perch, in flight, etc.:  Did not vocalize during any of my observations.----List similar species and how you eliminated them:  Easily separated from American Wigeon by rufous head and neck, buffy-white forehead disk, uniform gray flanks, lack of green on head.  The bird was closely examined for features consistent with American Wigeon and none were detected, eliminating the possibility of a hybrid.--Prior experience with this and similar species:  I have seen this species in several consecutive winters in Albuquerque NM, often at close range, once in Scottsdale AZ, and once at Bolinas Lagoon in northern California.----Optical equipment:--Viewed through Nikon Prostaff 20-60X82 Spotting Scope.----If photographed, please enclose a copy or attach digital copy to email.  --Photo equipment used:  Digiscoped using above mentioned spotting scope and a rather cheap Olympus digital camera.----Other observers who independently identified the bird (please list name and address if known):--None----Additional discussion:----References consulted:--None needed.----This report was written from notes made during _X_ after ___ observation (from memory).--If "after, from memory", approximately how long after the observation were notes first written:------Name: Carl G.
